Summary 176:
EU Ecolabel — rules on the labelling of food and feed products
EU ecolabel – rules on packaging and labelling
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2009 on the European Union Ecolabels
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
 
It sets out rules on labelling, labelling and the EU ecolabel*, the EU’s official name for products that meet certain essential environmental characteristics.
It aims to improve the quality of food, feed and animal feed and to ensure that products are marketed and sold in the EU with a high degree of eco-friendliness.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
food and feed;
animal feed and veterinary medicinal products;
medical devices;
consultancy services.
The European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) is responsible for administering the regulation. It is assisted by the European Bureau of Food Safety (EFSSA) and the European Commission. The European Union Bureau of Animal Health (Euratom) assists the Commission in the implementation of the regulation, and the Commission participates in its development and revision.
Ecolabel criteria are developed by a working group composed of representatives from the EU and non-EU countries. The working group meets at least twice a year. The Commission participates at least once a year in those meetings.
Each year, the working group draws up a list of products that are eligible for the EU Ecolablabel. It must highlight the criteria corresponding to the key environmental characteristics (e.g. water, air, soil, soil and water quality, etc.).
The Commission adopts the list and publishes it in the Official Journal of the EU. It also publishes a manual for potential users.
EU Eligible products must meet the following criteria:
good manufacturing practice (GMP);
good hygiene;
good product management;
environmental performance;
competent bodies.
Consultants must carry out a conformity assessment of each product before it can be awarded the EU colabel. The competent body must be independent of the competent body and must have the ability to carry out the conformity assessment.
If a product does not meet the criteria, it must be subject to a risk assessment to determine whether the product meets the criteria.
In addition, the competent bodies must ensure that:
the product has been tested and certified as organic;
the products have been tested in accordance with the requirements laid down in the regulation; and
the competent body has carried out the assessment and the product has not been altered or altered in any way that would cause it to fail to comply with the criteria;
there has been no significant change in the quality or environmental status of the product.
A European Commission working group is set up to develop the EU ECOLABEL criteria. The committee is chaired by the Commission and comprises representatives of the Commission, the European Environment Agency (EEA) and other interested parties.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
It has applied since 20 October 2009.
BACKGROUND
The EU eColabel is the EU system of labelling that applies to products that meets the essential environmental requirements of the Convention on the Conservation of Pollutants in Food and Feed (COPF).
For more information, see:
‘The European Union’ on the Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Organic: a product that meets all the essential requirements of COPF and that is not intended for human consumption. It does not contain any substances that are likely to harm the environment or that have an adverse effect on human health or the environment.
ACT
 			
  The European Parliament and the Council of 11 October 2009 on the Union EColabel (OJ L 183, 20.10.2009, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC, No 553/2009 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 177:
Protection of medicinal products from patent infringement
Protection against patent infringements
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2006 on the protection of medicines derived from basic patents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for the granting of a certificate of protection to medicinal products derived from a basic patent.
It aims to encourage the development of medicines that are the result of long-term, costly research.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all medicinal products which have been granted authorisation to be placed on the market as a medicinal product in the European Union (EU). It does not apply to products that have not been patented.
The certificate is granted to the holder of the basic patent or his successor in title. It is valid for a period of 5 years. The duration of the protection granted by the certificate must be such as to provide adequate effective protection. It may be revoked at any time by the competent authority of the EU country where the certificate holder surrenders it or withdraws it.
To obtain a certificate, the applicant must submit an application for an extension of the duration. The application must contain at least the following information: the name and address of the applicant;the number of the patent;the title of the invention;the name of the body responsible for authorising the product to be marketed in the EU and the number and date of the authorisation granted to place the product on the EU market.
An application for a certificate must also contain:
the product’s number and the date of authorisation;
the number and number of authorisations to apply for the certificate;
where applicable, the product identified in that authorisation.
A certificate may not be granted for more than 5 years, unless it is granted for a duration exceeding 5 years;
an annual fee must be paid by the holder.
EU countries may require that the certificate be subject to the payment of annual fees.
In addition, the certificate conferring the same rights as conferred by the patent and is subject to limitations and the same obligations as that conferred by that patent. The certificate may also be revoked if it is no longer effective or if it has expired or if the holder has not surrendered it or the product no longer meets the conditions laid down in the regulation.
Where an application is rejected, it must be published in the Official Journal. The notification must contain the following:
at the end of the period provided for in Article 13 of the regulation;
if the annual fee is not paid in time;
any indication that the application includes an application to extend the duration;
whether or not the product covered by a certificate has been withdrawn.
Expiry of the certificateThe certificate expires at the end, at least, of the 5-year period in which it was granted.
Authorisation to place on the European market
The authorisation must be granted in accordance with Directive 2001/83/EC. The authorisation may be withdrawn if the product is withdrawn or withdrawn for any number of reasons, including:
it has not been authorised;
it no longer satisfies the conditions set out in this regulation; or
the authorisation has expired.
Implementation
The European Medicines Agency (EMSA) is responsible for administering the certificate. It must:
ensure that the certificates are valid for at least 5 years and that they are valid throughout the EU;
notify the competent authorities of all EU countries of the validity and validity of the certificates;
provide them with the information they require in order to carry out their tasks.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It applies from 1 January 2007. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
 
  The regulation codifies and repeals Regulation No 1901/2006/EC (see summary).
For more information, see:
Protected medicinal products (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Basic patent: a patent granted by a patent holder to a pharmaceutical company for the purpose of protecting its products.
* Certificate of protection: a legal instrument granting the right to use a product for the purposes of patent protection.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 529/2006 of 21 December 2006 on the granting, on behalf of the European Community, of a Certificate of Protection to Medicinal Products derived from Basic Patents (codified version) (OJ L 136, 28.12.2006, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (Euratom) no 529/06/2006 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
last update 04.02.2016



Summary 178:
Convention on jurisdiction and enforcement of judgments in civil and commercial matters (Lugano Convention)
Convention of Lugano
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2016/852 — conclusion of the Convention on Jurisdiction and Enforcement of Judgments in Civil and Commercial Matters
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE CONVENTION AND THE DECISION?
The convention aims to ensure that judgments are recognised and enforced throughout the EU.
The decision concludes the convention on behalf of the European Community (now the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The parties to the convention agree to:
recognise and enforce judgments issued by a court in another EU country that is bound by the convention;
apply for a declaration of enforceability of judgments issued in that country;
appear before a court that has jurisdiction in the case of a dispute arising from a judgment issued in another country.
Judgments issued in a civil or commercial dispute may be declared enforceable in any EU country where they are recognised or enforced.
A judgment is recognised and enforceable where it is entered into by:
a court which has jurisdiction over the dispute;
the court with which an appeal is lodged; or
the courts of another country bound by this convention.
Appeals
An appeal must be lodged in a court with jurisdiction. The appeal must contain all the information necessary to establish that the judgment is enforceable. The court must give its decision without delay. The parties must also provide a copy of the judgment.
An application for a court to declare a judgment enforceable must be accompanied by the following information:
the name of the court which issued the judgment, the date of entry into force and the date on which the judgment entered into force.
the number of parties involved in the dispute and the nature of the dispute
the amount of money involved and the amount of time that has elapsed since the judgment was issued.
If the court in question has jurisdiction, it must grant the judgment and the judgment must be enforced in the country where the appeal was lodged.
Where a judgment has been issued in one party’s jurisdiction, the judgment in the other party must also be recognised in the court of jurisdiction of the country in which it was entered. The judgment must also contain a certificate of authenticity.
In addition, the parties to a dispute must provide the court with all the necessary information in order to determine whether or not the judgment has jurisdiction.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
 
   கமி  
The Convention entered into effect on 1 January 2017.
BACKGROUND
 ெ  কை  𝕷ற  ་  ̱ ང ె 
For more information, see:
‘Judges’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Judgments: judgments that are binding on a court, tribunal or other court of law. They may be issued by the court or tribunal of one party to a court of another party.
MAIN DOCUMENTS
Council Decision (EEC) No 852/2016 of 21 December 2016 on the conclusion of, and provisional application for provisional application of, the Conventions on Justice and Justice Enforcement in Civil And Commercial Matters (OJ L 347, 28.12.2016, pp. 1-8)
Council Resolution of 21 November 2016 concerning the conclusion, by the Council of the EU of the Community, of the Convention on Justice, Justice, Peace and Justice in Civil & Commercial Matters between the European Communities and the European Atomic Energy Community and its Member States, and repealing the Protocol on the Law of the Court of Justice of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland, and of the Protocol relating to the law of the State of Ireland, as amended by the Protocol of the Council concerning the law on the law and law enforcement in civil & commercial matters.
Successive amendments to the Council Resolution have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
Council Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 596/2014 of 22 December 2014 on the implementation of the Treaty on the Functioning of the Union and repealing Council Regulation (Euratom).
